## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics (nonlinear oscillations / dynamical systems)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration, and the features x (position), v (velocity), and t (time) match standard second-order ODE models for (possibly forced/damped) nonlinear harmonic oscillators. Common structures express dv_dt as a sum of restoring forces (functions of x), damping/friction (functions of v), and external/parametric forcing (functions of t, possibly multiplied by x or v).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear harmonic oscillator (SHO): dv_dt = -c0 * x (ideal linear restoring force, no damping/forcing)
- Viscously damped SHO: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (linear damping proportional to velocity)
- Driven damped SHO: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t + c4) (external periodic forcing)
- Constant bias / gravity offset: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 (equilibrium shift or constant acceleration term)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Quintic stiffness extension: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * x**5 - c3 * v (stronger anharmonic restoring force)
- Nonlinear (quadratic) damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v * Abs(v) (aerodynamic/drag-like dissipation in oscillators)
- Dry (Coulomb) friction oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * sign(v) (velocity-sign friction opposing motion)
- Duffing with nonlinear damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v - c3 * x**2 * v (amplitude-dependent dissipation)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (self-excited oscillation via negative damping at small |x|)
- Rayleigh oscillator form: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * (v - c2 * v**3) (self-excitation via velocity-dependent damping)
- Parametrically excited oscillator: dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (time-periodic stiffness; parametric resonance)
- State-dependent frequency / stiffness: dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * x**2) * x - c2 * v (effective stiffness increases/decreases with amplitude)
- Non-smooth stiffening (piecewise-like): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x * Abs(x) - c2 * v (approximate piecewise/impact stiffening using |x|)
- Nonlinear forced Duffing: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (canonical nonlinear forced oscillator)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative restoring force structure: if dv_dt depends primarily on x (and not v), the system is near-conservative with force derivable from a potential U(x), i.e., dv_dt ≈ -dU/dx.
- Odd restoring symmetry: terms like -c*x, -c*x**3, -c*x**5 suggest symmetric potentials U(x) with equilibria at x=0 and amplitude-dependent frequency.
- Linear damping fingerprint: a dominant -c*v term indicates viscous dissipation and exponential decay of small-amplitude oscillations in the unforced case.
- Amplitude-dependent damping: terms like -c*v*Abs(v) or -c*x**2*v indicate dissipation that grows with speed or amplitude (often yielding faster decay at large oscillations).
- Self-excitation / limit cycles: a factor (1 - c*x**2)*v (Van der Pol type) implies negative damping at small amplitude and positive damping at large amplitude, producing stable oscillations.
- Velocity-cubic damping competition: v - c*v**3 indicates growth at small |v| and saturation at large |v|, another route to limit cycles (Rayleigh-type).
- External periodic forcing: additive sin/cos terms in t imply entrainment, resonance peaks near the natural frequency, and possible multi-stability when combined with x**3.
- Parametric forcing indicator: time-periodic coefficients multiplying x (e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x) signal Mathieu/parametric-resonance behavior rather than direct forcing.
- Non-smooth friction: sign(v) (or sharp approximations to it) indicates stick-slip tendencies and non-sinusoidal waveforms, often requiring non-smooth regression primitives.
- Hardening vs softening inference: positive vs negative coefficients on x**3 (relative to -c0*x) correspond to frequency increasing vs decreasing with amplitude in Duffing-like models.
